y• tother syria may se wyll wynne pacifier conuaye hyther agayne tenne suche towny embatayled suche dyaloges • yr thomas hath vndertaken put hym selfe thaduenture alone agaynst • lette tary styll • wyll vtterly forswere mych mynded yet age cō mynge warynge vnwyeldy go thider geue thassaulte well walled towny wythout suche lusty company shalbe somewhat lykly lepe vp lytell lyghtly ¶the preface syr thomas chrysten reader man meruayle wene wyse menne wyll euer wold vouchsaufe bestow time makynge answere pacyfyers dyaloge consyderynge faynt feble reasonyng good fayth wel excuse selfe therin sodaynly went hande therwyth made breyde whā synnys considered lytell nede merueyled myne owne selfe repented hadde regarded boke wurthy without one worde let euyn alone ¶how good reders one thynge twayne specyally moued make answere happed fall hand therwyth spende lese lytell tyme make mater playne vnto thynge shall shew ¶as soone myne apologye one come abrode anone herde worde wrothe therwyth yet mynde man cause neyther precher pacyfyer none heretyke neyther hadde spoken selfe good folke catholyke fayth without reproch reprofe mannes person wyllyng man harme yt wyllyng mende wyllyng nought styll cause wroth wyth hym self wote well ¶but wolde serue wroth wyth howbeit theyr causelesse anger dyd gretely greue farre vnreasonable loke reasonable myndes vnreasonable menne ¶but herde shortely thykke threfolde penny went wurke answeres makyng diuerse dyuerse great cūnyng mē trayuayle great moūtayne hyllys herd myche speche made almoste euery weke ferforth laste tolde trouth vnto one lytell pyece one greate cunnynge man made long answere twelue whole shetys paper wryten nere gyther smale hande ¶but good fayth coulde laugh pyece sure cūnyngest man coulde come therto neyther tenne shetys tenne query neyther wryte nere coulde sholde neuer answere well ¶for pyece answere yt myne apalogye make se vnto certayne sermon wherin dyaloge towched wrytynge agaynst tyndals false translacyon wherin also defended agaynst confutacyon tyndals wyse chapyter agaynst dyaloge laboreth proue worde chyrche chapyter neuer towcheth ye poynt sermon defended hym walketh wyde ¶it tolde say answere made place shyfte founde remanaunt coulde fyrst poynt herde saye deuysed reherse precher spake poysoned brede rehersed hym wrong spake moulden brede pyece tolde yt new answere reasoned length set forth luste • ¶but come boke abrode onys shall sone abate corage fyrst syth taketh recorde yt sayd mouldy brede yf brynge wytnesse also said poysoned bred wytnesse stande hym none stede proue hym sayd bothe ¶secundly shall proue sayd poysened brede meanes men shall se reason yt though tother possyble yet farre vnlykely ¶finally shal ferther proue though ye man sayd poysened brede onely moulden brede yet shall proue saye case stode poysened brede moulden brede yet poysened worde ¶heryng therfore gaye boke made xii shetys paper lacked ouerloking many mo ī hand ye shortly shold come lyke husband whose wife trauayle herkeneth euery hande whyle fayne wold good tydynges syth myche herde sore trauayle many cunnynge aboute dyuerse answeres longed theyr longe laboure se good spede fayre babe borne trauayled ¶and great hyllys thus trauailed longe weke ester tyll myche afore myche • ma good houre came god wold ye one broughte bed sore labour laste deliuered dede mouse moder yet grene good soule hath nede good kepyng woman wote caudell serueth agaynst throwes ¶now boke came myne handes sawe maner fashyon therof two thynges onely moued wryte medle wyth yt one sawe therin folowed pursewed selfe shrewed malicyouse intent purposed fyrst boke diuysyon wyt make thordynaryes fere slaunder oloquye seue theyr dutyes vndone lette heretyques alone ouer wyth euyl newe chaunge good old lawes labour putte heretyques corage therby decaye fayth ¶this dede specyall poynte made wryte yet agayne yet founde lytle reason hys reasonynge thought yt sholde nede thys wyste well euer wyt wold conferre compare gether wordes hys answere wyth wordes myne apologye sholde sone perceyue hys answeres euyn dull dede ¶but thenne nother thynge consydered yt whyche poynte vnprouyded myghte soon deceyue reader yt pacyfyer hath place put myne owne wordes yt pleased hym yet hathe moste parte vsed prety crafte mysse reherse mater leue wordes oute ye besydes man hath place lefte oute owne mysse rehersed make reader wene reprouynge theym hadde wryten wronge ¶now supposed remedy thingꝭ make answere thre foure leues wyth onely poyntynge reader place wyth wrytynge lefe shold fynde mater wordꝭ one redde trouthe sholde shewe yt selfe ¶but whyle thus mynded went hys answere dialoge foūden way wyth walkynge fro kepynge maner order therwyth makynge seke longe one place yt saw wel shold soner answere hym new fynde many thynges place sholde seke ¶i made therfore day • answere se suche place yet happed finde haue remytted reader vnto myne apologye redye findyng haue nōbred • lefe yet haue folke done somwhat se wel surely many men nowe dayes delycate readynge lothe labour fare bokes womē fare theyr primer though content saye tyme ye fyftene psalmys ouer yt psalmys passyon yf fynde al fayre lette order length yet wyll rather leue theym vn sayde turne backe seke theym partyes theyr prymer ¶and therfore leste reader myghte happe boke place thapologye myche necessarye longe wyth myche sekynge fortuned fynd ease reders labour make open vnto hym haue put also myne answere ye yet ouer thys thynges moste weyghte haue put thys boke hys owne wordes shall good reader wythout payne sekynge haue mate • playn open afore yien ye shal well se loue lyght lesse thenne thys pacyfyer wolde fayne walke darke darke mater hys auauntage euen y veryly lyghte lyke wyse myne cō mende answere compendyouse breuite therof shortnesse nothinge therin enuye mannes prayse lyke man make shorter course lacketh hys legges cā man make shorter boke lacketh wel wordes mater yet place conferred well gether feblenesse answere shall appere shall lese prayse shortnesse yt shall wel sene yt sayth nothyng purpose shall eu • ry wise man thynke hys boke longe gether ye may wel perceyue dede let v leue preface fall vnto mater fyrste chapyter fyrste chapyter toucheth thre thinges one haue deceyued hys hope haue myne apologye dyuysed conuenyent wayes reforme redresse dyuysyon betwene temporaltye spyrytualty whyche poynte wyll answere touchyng hys seconde chapyter tother poynt syth neuer found faute worke myne whyche • ettis neuer redde none merueleth mych therfore make obieccyon agaynste namely worke whych wolde name apologye whyche name sygnyfyeth sayth answere defence ¶now good man declareth thynge apologye y sayth yt answere defence whych cause meruaileth wold boke wryte agaynste treatyse hys neuer hadde thynge wryten worke myn though therfore wrytynge agaynste worke wold wise agre name boke myghte answere hym touchynge boke incident shew 100 lefe sayde boke pryncypall mater therfore many noughty thynges touche fewe suche wyse dissembled meruaile myche wherfore shold meruayle wold ye worke name answere defence wryte agaynst worke nothynge wrote agaynst myn thynge wryte agaynst wordes answere defence dede thenne though defēce self yet cause meruayle gone boke called myne apologye yt requyred ye nature ye name yt answere defence myne owne selfe suffyceth yt myne owne makynge answere defence title caluicium sinccii moria erasmi name conuenyent bokes theyres though mater bokes sygnifyed name onely pertein vnto sinecius erasmus peraduenture neyther theym al may boke well bere name answere defence yf answere defence made though yt made folke one pyece therof made ¶so yt myne apology answere defence onely formare bokes wherin new brethern began fynde certayn fa • te ouer self parte wherin touche boke dyuysyon answere defence many good worshyppefull folke agaynst malycyouse slaunder obloquye generally sette forth many salse sayes sedycyouse boke ¶the selfe pyece y also answere defence good olde longe approued lawes bothe thys realme whole corp chrystendome lawes thys pacyfyer boke dyuysyon thencoragynge heretyques parell catholyque faythe wyth warme wordes colde reason oppugneth ¶and finally myche many good vertuouse folke began vpō yll boke dyuysyon haue ryght euyl opinyon maker selfe playne confessyon trew faith toke take yet mā good catholike therfore many place myne apology lay faute fro man hym self vnto wyly shrewes deceyued hym myne apologye answere also defence ye person pacyfyer hym selfe goeth nowe confute yt y remanaunt hys answere one pyece thyng appeyreth poynte myne apologye yt trouthe thys poynte goeth moste nere thys answere hathe made suche maner wyse shall haue nowe myche hadde make wyse man wene euer hym selfe ment well yet wyll leue yt styll wyll putte hym false wyly shrewes though man dothe saye contrarye therto hym selfe ¶and man denieth thynge hym selfe maketh yt lykely trew thynges playne appere nought rather taketh mater whole vppon hym suffreth parte layed hym man haue importune pryde goddes grace hath elles yt sure sygne good token suche good symple soule soone may deceyued se wit serueth hym better wolde rather appere malycyouse vnwyse ¶but nowe haue proued hym name apologye may serue well euery pyece boke nowe wyll somwhat se mater boke agree well wyth name therof mean hys boke dyuysyon boke name mater agree gether well meane hys newe boke nowe hande wyth whyche boke appereth fyrste fronte fyrst lefe y named salem bizance therin hundred syx leues many boke scante fully fyftene thynge agree wyth name ¶nowe yf wyll saye communycacyon betwene salem bizance y bye mater besyde remanaunt bytwene theyre talkynges y boke thanne y yt worse hathe hys booke neuer name ¶more ouer yf yt thenne sholde none thre laste chapyters bere name wytte xxii xxiii xxiiii chapyter lyke wyse calleth begynnyng theyr communycacyon byfore hys mater introduccyon sholde haue called thre chapyters mater extraduccyon ¶ yet wote well maye saye therof begynnynge boke theyre fyrste communycacyon y called introduccyon y intyteled vpon leuys yet ende introduccyon byfore fyrst chapyter man sayeth hym selfe persone bizance hathe made yet none introduccyon meaneth thys tell yf meane make men wene salem bizance two englyshe men dede spake wordes selfe wythout worde hys ¶but nowe bycause sheweth hym selfe connynge greke wordes vppon thys worde apologye fyndeth afore sayde faute wyth myne apology though ouersene obserued ye nature apology lette v se howe well hym selfe begynnynge calleth hys booke dyaloge obserueth nature propertye dyaloge ¶in ye thyrd lefe salē sheweth self desyrouse se pacifyers answere bizance answereth shall cause yt wryten dyaloge worde worde yt come handes thou shalt wyth good wyll haue yt thou shalt vnderstande hys answere begynneth nexte chapyter hereafter ensuynge contynueth place shall shewe yt endeth ¶consyder good reader introduccyon doth bryng rehersal cōmunicacyon hadde byfore communycacyon present thenne lette hym shewe euer hathe herde hys lyfe two men theyre talkynge gether diuyde theyr present cōmunycacyon chapytres poynte onely farre fro nature dialoge also al reason chylde wolde wene haue handeled thynge chyldyshely ¶also bizāce telleth salem pacyfyers answere shall wryten theyr dyaloge wyt theyr communycacyon sawe euer lyke sawe euer thyng wryten communycacyon wrytyng planted among wordes spoken ¶and reason hath yt tell hym aboute theyr communycacyon pacifyers wordes shal begynne shall ende • though salem talkyng wyth bizance hadde wyt perceyue bizance speketh hym self redeth hym pacyfyers wordes wryten ¶also straunge monstrose beste maketh bizance salem pacifier answere whyle maketh thoughe salem coulde neyther perceyue hed tayle yf hym selfe poynted hym stycke ouer bizance sayth wyll wryte theyr dialoge yt wyt theyr present • talkynge soone cometh handes word yet wryteth euyn neyther goeth fette maketh man come thyther hym bryng proprely deuysed ¶than stand styll fyrste mete strete lykelyhed folke comenly mete mete aduenture answere perused readynge wherof standeth ye lest foure fyue howres trow lytell ouersene stande styll aboute readynge stande styll twayne whyle byzance se theyr talkynge cōmunicacyō wrytynge yf bizance wryte fast warraunt wurke weke wekes ende whan xxi chapyters wryten bizance xxii chapyter geueth salem warnynge answere pacyfyer ended ye pacifier fole prudently deuysed ellys wolde salem wene theyr owne talkynge together tother thre chapyters mouth ben styll nothynge ellys onely bizances wrytynge el wold also salem haue thought owne wordes exhortacy ō agaynst great turke rehersynge exposycyon apocalyps bene styll pacyfyers wordꝭ agaynst myne apology ¶and finally ende shew could write onely prose endeth whole booke wyse gloryouse ryme thus gloryonse trynite haue kepyng bothe maketh bizance praye mo theym two maner good manne • ryme mustarde maker cambrydge yt wont pray hym self wyfe chyld grace make good mustarde ¶and thus se good reader yt man cūning greke wordꝭ yt shortely fynd ye fawt fayle ye nature apologye hym selfe dyaloge well cōserueth propertye dialoge expresseth naturally yt could neuer done naturally though wrote euyn naturall dede ¶but semeth haue meruayled whan redde myne apology wolde make obieccyons agaynst wurke whyle neuer wrote thynge agaynste booke myne good fayth yf wolde neuer haue bene hasty somwhat peraduenture ye lesse leste myghte haue semed desyre reuengynge myne owne dyspleasure excyted therto nowe worldely profyte growynge thereby mych lesse cause good man thynke wolde take labour wryte agaynst wurke wyst whose yf leste wyse semed selfe suche thynges therin god wold geue thāke geue mē warnynge well ware ¶and sayeth wyll touch euery thyng partycularly take order order answerynge therunto let ī boke vse order beste maye serue purpose thought yet thynke selfe toke playne open way whan chapyters whiche wold answere perused al waye euery thynge order whiche order foloweth shall fynd self shall good reders iudge vpon ye ende yet meane whyle fyrste face semeth wyth lepynge order meaneth make mater playne ¶nor sayth wyll answere neyther auoydynge tedyousnes trouth yf haue semeth signyfye bysynesse thynke somwhat tedyouse hym answere gether ¶finally saith supposeth make appere hys answeres consideracyons declaracyons myne obieccyons lytell pondered fyrste argumentes made agaynste lawes wherby fayth preserued heresyes kept vnder argumentes answeres wyll neuer able mayntayne ye remanaunt good faith better maye make innocent mynde appere gladder greate deale wyll therof nothynge purpose therin thys present booke ferther make clerely perceyue well euer frere baron bygan go abrode therin wold seme saye contrary byddeth loke better vppon mater shall fynde otherwyse dede better lokyng theron fynd somwhat otherwyse fynde ye tyme encreace speke mych veryly yf knewe suche great cause thys man setteth forth trewe whych knowe false knewe wayes reforme wolde vse wayes towarde sedycyouse slaunderouse bookes haue expressely declared myne apologye neyther neuer dyd neuer entende put abrode prente vnder colour reformacyon fawtes hatefull odyouse eyther tone parte tother specyally many onys yf trewe lykely remedyed one parte whyle remaynynge lytell remedyed shold • make eyther parte odyouse bothe partes infamouse amonge suche yf suche wold gladde reioyce mych euyl spoken bothe ¶and thys saye though trewe wolde mych lesse vse maner makyng rehersall thynges wherof many false vntrew many also tryfeles chyefe thynges thys pacyfyer desyreth haue reformed lawes redy well made whyche wold haue made wurse haue ben wyse men well deuysed repressyng heresyes perleament thys realme generall counsayle chrystendome deuyseth chaunged chaunge whyche desyreth though goddes grace desyreth shold yet dowte dede sholde turne thencoragynge heretykes encreace heresyes wyth mynysshement decaye catholyke chrysten fayth wherupon wold fayle whych almyghty god kepe v greuouse indygnacyon vpon v therfore god kepe v suche reformacyons ¶now laye therfore greate fawte blame boke vntrew sayes vnder colour ceacynge dyuysyon excyte set forth dyuysyon yf selfe coulde ceace whan suche bookes make myche lyke yf wold say ought man blame hym wolde burne vp nother mannes howse wolde buylde agayne ¶and therfore thys good reason putteth remembraunce answere man myne made one myche fashyon sometyme one called clyffe man wel knowen mayster henry patenson clyffe hadde bene many yeres mad age taken hym rage metely well waxen harmlesse among folke clyffes hed came tyme madnesse imagynacyons agaynst image heretykes haue theyr sadnesse lyke whych fledde ranne awaye fell thefte caught pulled late vpō londō brydge thinmage blessed martyr saint thomas clyffe vpon brydge vppon tyme fyll talkynge vnto image blessed lady suche blasphemyes ye deuyll putte hys mouth dayes bloweth ye mouthes many heretykes whyche seme neuer sad yet madde sette hande vppon chylde arme brake ye necke afterwarde whan honest men dweller vppon brydge came home myne howse blamed clyffe asked hym wherfore brake chyldys necke lady arme whan clyffe hadde herde began loke well erenestly vpon thē lyke man sadnesse grauyte asked theym tell • hys amonge haue yet sett hys hed agayne ꝙ ꝙ clyffe ye masse shame speke ¶ euyn thus answereth thys good man whyche hys sedycyouse sayes set forth diuysyō breke chyldys necke rekeneth shame fynde fawte wyth hym ye brekynge yf selfe coulde glew together agayne ¶and therfore sayth sholde haue proued cause layeth cause dyuysyon cause dyuysyon ellys sholde haue deuysed remedyes albe haue answered hym therin redy yet thys saye therin ferther haue proued wel clerely yt chyef cause yt sayeth layd vntrewly wytte mysse handelyng people theyr destruccyon vppon suspycyon heresye whyche cause yf trewe yt y false weyghty well wurthy layde mater dyuysyon whyle trewe yet suche kookes beynge blowen aboute euery parte realme trewe maye well mysse happe make dyuysyon whyle dweller euery quarter aboute credence geuen booke may fyrste face wene though dwell selfe yet wene saye al place wherof though shall leysoure perceyue contrary wyth serche yet aske ferther questyon shall byleue styll rumour onys begonne semed tollerable wolde good faythe haue bene lothe haue towched theym eyther whyche whyle hys consideracyons declaracyons goeth shew ment none harme wyll therin mych hynder hym gladde rather forther hym thexcuse hys menynge dyd haue sayd euyn myne apologye though glad excuse mynde menyng yet excuse vnwyse folowynge false wyly counsayle doynge iii chapyter iii chapyter cō teynyng hys secōd pray yt wyth hym ¶but yet sayth thende chapiter endeuour selfe myche oppresse al wyll shew suche thynges spyrytualtye dede suche haue made suche lye haue tolde yt theym oppressyon let hym proue one let hym call one xx ꝓue none wote well cā good reders let hym beleued therafter ¶more ouer sayth mynde proue yt intollerable defaute people mysse iudgynge clergy thinke haue cause therin leue theym though whole cause pryncypall defaute temporaltye wherin sayth iugement farre deceyued poynte good reder sayth somwhat yf sayde trew sure yf thought wrote herein trewe wysedome wolde sholde haue wryten myne owne wordes yf fered yt wolde founden false honestye wolde sholde haue leste hys owne wordes oute veryly good reader seke thys seuen yere shall myne apologye fynde suche wordes myne shall fynde farre contrarye wote well suche place shewe men vnreasonable wolde take thys thynge thynge suche reherse hys bryngynge forthe reasonable cause dyuysyon saye place pacyfyer mysse sayeth people people myche reasonable take yt therfore belyeth agayne ¶and also let hym shewe forth one place whyche say whole faute pryncypal faute eyther tēporaltye byleue hym better nother mater meane whyle tyll brynge forthe ellys fynde yt self ye may reason lest wyse mater byleue better thenne hym wil neuer desyre byleue one day lenger haue neyther sayde pryncypall faute tone ye tother thus hath made thre lye one chapyter iiii chapyter iiii chapyter begynnyng viii lefe fyrst sheweth diuersyte betwene sample put ye 94 lefe myne appologye pacyfyer betwene man hys wyfe thyng resemble vnto wytte hys owne boke maketh lyke pacifycacyon betwene temporaltye spyrytualtye ¶but surely dyfference putteth semeth pore wyt greatly payre parte yf sayth yt husbande wold loth heare euyl spoken wyfe therfore wil suche pacyfyer thanke wyll tell hym suche tale neyghbours temporaltye wyll glad heare harme spoken spyrytualtye yt myche worse done wryte openly temporaltye suche thynges spyrytualtye fede nuryshe suche euyll delyte openly spyritualtye beynge sayde lyke wyse affectyonate fautes temporaltye eyther howe yt good fayth saye yf shold belye hym syde wyllyngely greatly passed boundes ouersyght vnware hath thynges slaundered ye temporalty ¶then sheweth farther wherfore wrote thynges englyshe though iohn̄ gerson wrote theym laten wherin say trouth layeth cause suffycyent wherfore iohn̄ gerson wrote latyne whyther laye cause suffycyent wherfore hym selfe shold rather haue let alone wryte englishe agaynst counsayle iohn̄ gerson hym selfe touched myne apology leue self good reades cōsyder wil myche stryue agaynste excuse greatly shall nede thinke syth al excuse amounteth ment laye men redynge prestes fautes englishe myght put remembraunce mende specially bycause sayth euen chapiter litle afore temporaltye myche delyteth theym thē goth farther ye chapiter boke dyuisyon wold haue semed betwene tēporaltye spyrytualtie haue spoken indifferently haue told theyr fautes parti • • gally ordynarye therof yt semeth conuenyent ordynarye sende hym man yet notoryousely knowen detected heretyque knowe farther whether yt trew hath reported yf fynde yt trewe suffycyent profe hys owne confessyon wyll reformed yt semeth couenyent vppon wytnes p • nyshed hath de •• ued yf wyll ordynary secretely reformed yt semeth good yt depart without •• n penaunce conuenient ther b • ne mater wyll cōmytte yt ¶ consyder good reader cōmodile order se speketh one speketh wordes herers seme heresye taketh informeth thordinary doth thordynarye nowe may perceyue progresse deuyce though mo thān one herd hym mo twayne tenne eyther yet wold ordinary shold send fyrst assay herd wyll saye y asked questyon thynge hym selfe • ̄t therby haue wyt say yt ment wordꝭ suche thynge meanynge soundeth none heresy wit heretykes ynough haue y mater answered thā ye wote wel wyly heretyque wyse order may bolde gloses redy proued saye wyll wyll ordynarye maye sende hym laye • eretycal wordes charge consyder vpon cyrcumstaunce dealynge suche talkynge peraduenture diuerse place vsed whether ment hym selfe declareth yt ment teache thynge spake hepe declaracyō store scuse fyrst poynte alone thys good mannys order yf yt surely obserued ynough fyl whole towne shortely ful heresyes ¶than goth farther second poynte yf spake heresyes wyl asked questyon auowe theym yet shal herd hym resorte vnto thordynarye go fetche wytnesses fyrste whome yf felow folysh confesse frantike auow good mā geueth theym leue go tell thordynarye tale accuse hym nowe yf haue wytte byfore wytnesses lye saye neuer sayd theym saye wil saye mate • yet saufe ynough agayne shall neuer nede euer ordynary worde hym let hym go forthe vse fashyon styll many companyes cometh ye wote wel hurt yf euery man whome speketh heresye secretly secretely wolde make mo heretyques shold secretely enforme ordynarye sholde vpon xx suche secrete informacyons afterwarde call hym forthe openly vppon theyre open deposycyons openly make hym abiure beare fagot accurse hym hys obstynacye whole yeres sufferaūce fynally immedicable malyce desperate wreche delyuere hym seculare handes fagotte sholde beare hym thys cruell delynge ordynarye mysse handelynge good honest man heresye ¶and yet goeth farther lytle though holde yt auow heresyes afore witness thordynarye sholde yet procede agaynst hym openly speke hym secretely though auow theym hym selfe yet sholde thys good mannys aduyse procede agaynste • hym ordynarye meanes openly let hym departe wythoute open penaunce yf felowe wyse laste rather wolde come therto saye wyl amēde wyll say thynges al conuenyent farther done wil sayth • emyt vnto men yt myche nede dede yt yf order deuyse • h wel obserued farre forthe goeth wene worlde coulde well deuyse farther suffycyentely reforme remedy myschyefe hys charytable deuyse wolde ¶how beste therin deuyseth order thing stande euer tyme saith sayth daungerouse tyme whyle thys dyuyuysyon contynueth ¶but nowe yt good reader whether tyme daungerouse speketh whether tyme suche dyuysyon maketh sure saye euyn tyme heresyes begyn growe great deale faster haue bene wont tymes past therfore tyme mych worse vse • uch order thā nother time wherin many fewer yf pacyfyer wyl nowe peasyble deuise order y• al myscheuous factyous folke shold suffered peace shall wyth peasyble order yf yt obserued brynge worlde case good peasyble folke fayne wold lyue peace shold inquiete vnrestful wreches without rufle lyue peace longe ¶were wise order wene wold like wise deuyse theuys softe charytable fashyon deuiseth heretikis wyt men shold hym stolen horse robbed house go geue hym monicyon fyrst yf saye dyd yt wolde take mater saufe say wolde haue order waye kepte onely suche dayngerouse tymes many folke wolde fall thefte yt good spare theim speke fayre suffer theym tyll wolde waxe fewer selfe vse agaynste theym lawis old order wold thys wyse waye trowe well thefte sothe yt awaye farre vnwyse farre agaynst reason heresy eyther theft murder maner cryme ¶and surely semeth y• calleth dayngerouse tyme vseth daungerous worde fere ordynaryes wyth wolde make worlde wene heretyques many stronge thordynaryes myght nowe theyre dutyes subduynge heresyes wythoute great daungeour wherin great daungeour yet shall dout kynges grace day longe mote y parynge apple howe yt wyl denye hym thys inded yf suche daungerouse wordes dyuysyon may make thordynaryes aferd theyre owne shawdow whyle yt may grow daunger laste ¶but goeth • e farther nother remedye truste god shall neuer nede truste god neuer shall thys realme suche great personage fall heresye thordynarye dare procede accordynge law agaynste hym howe yt case yt shold happen • good man prouideth remedy say trouth wel wyt thordynary sholde haue recourse vnto kynge hyghnes vppon petycyon made vnto hym informacyon geuyn hym maye doute wolde wyth royall assystence prouyde meane suffycyent yt course lawe myght ꝓcede ¶this wel deuised plaieth good kow geueth v • good galon mylke thā shal se howe playeth shrewde know agayne turneth ouer payle euyn wyth hele vppon good deuise forth addeth shrewd sayēg yt longe opynyon amonge peple ordinaryes theyr offycers wil geue lytght credence vppon informacyons made theym heresye wyll noyse theym complayned • heretyques dew examynacyon behalfe long wyll peple grudge peraduēture kynge geue hys assystence redyly haue attached wolde yf herde ordynaryes noysed man heretyque wythout dew examynacyon rehersed ¶if good man myche wyt se wel lacketh wold wax euyll content hym shold one conceyue opynyon kinges graciouse hyghnes grace wold thynge remysse geue royall assystence vnto thordinaries ye attachīg suspect heresy longe hys grace herde thordynaryes noysed man heretyque wythoute suche dewe examynacyon man afore rehersed kynges hygh prudence wel perceiueth sholde forbere tyl tyme sholde suche thynge sayde theym yt almoste myche say shold geue asystence agaynste heretykes tyl al heretykes gone neuer shall lacke suche false sedycyouse fame agaynste ordynaryes longe heretyques sowe suche sedycyouse bokes dyuysyon vntrew sayes blowe yt farther abrode vntrouth false fame hath ben kinges honorable counsayle late well playnely proued redy vppon sondry suche false complayntes kinges gracyouse commaundement examyned thynge notoriousely knowen haue also selfe myne apologye spoken thereof synnys boke gone abrode hath ben lyke wyse lordes well playnely proued mo mater fresshe water wessheth awaye mater yet goeth euer water ouer goosys backe thynge man man make synke vnto skynne maye one fele euer shaketh playne proues fethers say say contrary prety proper way therfore thus se good reders mānes deuicys order taken suche speke heresyes vicyouse haue neuer fayre fleryng fyrste face yet whā cōsydered well founden farre worse thā nought yet mynded maye se haue examyned farre sauynge euyn whyle writynge chapyter leue worde brought thys deuyce order heresye folke self haue knowen specyally well commended ¶but yet wyll thys man say effecte dothe mayster wyll say thys euery thynge man speketh whiche yf obstynately wolde holde w • heretyke inough iudge euery man heretyke doth maner speke ¶i wyll thys tyme varye good man dyspute hym vppon trouth ye tale many maner way spekynge man maye speke therof dysprayse therof wyll saye hym tale lyke neuer trewe yet semeth mych better englysshe prented booke ¶for yf thynke necessary wryte bycause folke thynketh necessary lerne eyther meneth nede whiche spyrytuall iudges el comen people iudges veryly haue knowen knowe many yet knewe neuer none symple wyt farre vnlerned wyt lernyng perceyue man wurste theym wyste greate dele better perteyned vn theyr parte theyr dutye suche poyntes doth thys good man ¶than yf saye putteth bycause though knowe mysse vse contrary therby misse handle kynges people put theym cruell punyshement vniustely aske hym proueth lye trew therto ye wote well wyll brynge forth playne profe playn trouth mater old thre wurshypfull wytnesses whiche stand yet vnsworne wyt saye say folke say hath brought forth two whome maketh semeth bothe wytnesses iudges good sely sowle symkyn salem ryght honest neyghbour brother byzance well content yt fyue wytnesses sworē wel examined know thyngꝭ reporte spyrytuall iudges shall speke proue set layed vnto theyr charge yf fynde suche many theyr dealynge cruell vniuste man maketh thynge well towarde content ye shall byleue remanaūt wurse yet yt wysse somwhat content byleue also man cause necessary occasion profytable put yt tale bate makynge boke ¶but mene whyle laye agaynste hym yt point agaynst fyue wurshypfull wytnesses dede reporte ye gretest moste honorable temporall lordes kynges honorable counsayle ryght wurshypfull temporall men whiche gracyouse commaūdement kinges hyghnesse haue examyned dyuerse suche complayntes suit ye partyes thē selfe theyr frendes haue theruppon founden complayntꝭ false thordynaryes haue done ryght wyth great fauour ¶and therfore thys poynte treuthe beynge substancyally proued vppon syde hys fyue forenamed wytnesses tother syde sette fyue strawes therfore good reders poynt puttynge pyece hys boke diuisyon neyther necessyte profyte excepte eyther necessary profytable sow euyll sede agaynste good folke vntrew reprouable slaunder hys owne wrytynge vnder colour mēnes vnproued wordꝭ ¶than resteth farre se one cause byhynde yt shold excuse hym thynge profytable people know though man lyghtnesse passyon growynge ignoraunce frayltye speke • alke heresyes lybertye yet yf defende opinatyuely shold taken heretyke therby deryly good reader yf thys tale trewe yet wolde wene sayde tale vnto people good vnwryten wryten great dele better ¶as thys good man man ellys let theym wryte lyste saye thynke good neuer badde dede durste conscyence vse thys fashyon wrytynge concernynge heresye wolde vse wrytynge boke wherof wolde speke eyther treason felony excepte necessary occasyon sholde happely dryue therto good occasyon hys booke dyuysyon droue good man therto ¶if agayne reade lyncolns ine hande wyth statute touched treason felonyes wolde let loke seke reherse whyther heyghnouse wordes spoken agaynst prynce onely spekynge taken treason ¶nor wolde let lyke wyse declare founde casy • whyche man though toke mannes horse agaynst law sholde yet iudged felon therby wolde onely bolde tell wolde also bolde french peculiare lawys realme leue wyth wrytynge yet wold reken selfe sor • ouer sene yf suche thynges wolde scole speke redyng wolde englysh euery mannys hand put abrode prent necessyte therin tother ye place court cōpanies must nedes taught oute whyche companyes must taken shalbe made iudges iudge comon people tolde tale shall farre se many folke lytell good rather great harme perceyuyng thinges thynge perell ferede may waxe therin neglygent lesse ferynge ye lesse dayngeour may soone steppe therfore haue wyste ere thys iudges great wysedome great open audyence haue hadde occasyon speke hyghe mysseprisyon treason forbere yet sayenge suche thynges wolde haue letted speke among selfe ¶if man wold happely thynke well done euery mā taught wollde aledge therfore know surely thynge wolde make hys behauour hygh treason heresye though wolde aduenture euer vnder yet wold peraduenture ware kepe hym selfe well many man though byleue shall abyde greate payne purgatory hys venyall synnes dothe greate dylygence forberynge yet ye feare perpetuall payne hell taketh greate hede kepe hym selfe frome synnes surely knoweth mortall ¶as suche venyall synnes folke fraylty comenly fall man almoste tyme wythout theym though profyte wolde yf men dyd wene mortall drede therof coulde make menne vtterly forbere theym yet syth wyll men wyll vtterly forbere knowlege trouth necessary leste euery tyme suche veniall synne dede wenyng mortall doyng dede wyth conscyence mortall synne myghte make mortall dede ¶but kynde veniall synnes mych custume may easyly forborne neuer founde wyse man remembraūce wold eyther wryte teche comune peple exactly say though thus farre yet dedely synne wyll suche thynges syth veniall synne self drawyng toward ye dedely rather leue people dowt drede dedely synne thereby cause kepe selfe farre tellynge theym venyall synne make lesse aferde come myche ner • r mortall synne assaye nere canne come tyll come laste nere brynke hys fote slyppeth downe falleth • rypture saith quiamat periculum peribit illo loueth perell shall perysshe ¶nowe heyghnouse wordes spekynge agaynste prynce talkynge heresye agaynste knowen catholyque fayth thynges lyke commen veniall synnes thynges bothe twayne whyche theym maye myche easely forbere therfore profyte vnto people thynke rather perell therin thanne lesse ¶the iudgꝭ parte se punysshement passe grauyte offence therfore shall comon people take none harme though selfe concernynge treason heresye fall suche bokes myncyng suche mater dyspute howe farre maye go forwarde theym wythout extreme daynger perell shall better kepe selfe greater yf fere greater kepe selfe well lesse ¶but surely suche tale tolde vn people geuyn euery man woman auenture prented englysshe bookes abrode may geue suche boldenesse talkynge thys man thys xiiii chapyter dothe tell theym therin mych perell many man wolde wene maye myche harme bothe vnto selfe vnto selfe lytell lesse feare maye soone fall ferther dyd euer wolde haue done sholde whome sholde happen fynde holy saynt hierome sayth better leue thynges vnknowen perell lerne theym ¶to men also maye man thereby myche harme man bolde talkynge heresyes wherby maketh men fyrste take lyght lytell lytell byleue whyle boldely speke hym nothynge reproue may mych harme making many fal ye fayth though fallen hym selfe shold hylde tonge though secretely harte starke heretyke dede ¶and therfore surely good reader euer man ment hys owne secrete mynde fashyon doctrine yet mynde playnely thynge people myche perylouse profytable booke dyuysyon euyll putte euyll repeted agayne ¶now referreth remanaunt mater concernyng heresye vnto theym better skyl desyieth aske done wyth suche speke heresyes none heretykes theyr harte surely yf euer suche case sholde happen shold nede make serche poynte wolde wyth good wyll loke suche necessyte inough yf sholde happe talke heresyes declare vnto theyr ordynaryes whome ferther charge apperteyneth make therupon ferther serch suche maye theruppon maye ferther fynde therof ferther therin thys man hym selfe canneth therin thynge se lytell skyll wolde hadde lesse medeled therwith tell teache peple fyrst hys booke dyuysyon afterwarde thys booke agayne maye speke talke heresyes well inough wythout daynger perell suche spekynge lawfully taken heretyques wyth whiche tale though trewe doth yet lytell good vsyng spekyng heresyes yf fully proue man heretyque yet may make hym ye wote well heresye hys harte ryghte sore suspecte oure sauyour saythe hym selfe ex habundantia cordis o loquitur mouth speketh suche thynges harte plentuouse haboundeth therfore saye though neyther defende obstynately precysely proued heretique secrete harte yet maye open wordes suche though spoken tel maner passyon sore suspycyon wordes hath brought hym selfe maye well wyth good reason compelled abiure therin wysse great honesty great profyte neyther yet al profyte se come thys good mannes doctryne ¶and thynge good mā bosteth chapiter seconde syde xliiii lef deny though goten therby great ouer hande ye mater yet wold good reders saue length let hym perceyue thys ouersyghte ignoraunce another maner touchynge thynge bosteth denye hym wolde make hym loke lyttell better euyn vppon summa rosella mych allegeth hym selfe ¶and lefe syde maketh certayne certyfycate though bysshoppe hadde sente hym commyssyon enquyre knoweth one heretyke realm worde dede mary wolde meruayle myche yf dyd yt muste nedes long ere knowe man lytle suspycyouse mater heresye though sholde theym talke heresye hym yet bycause though heare theyr mouthes speke yet perdyelo • oke vnto theyre harte se thynke knoweth also whyther yf asked well ferde wolde holde yt opynatyuely elle • rather burned beare fagotte say sayde yt al passyon ignoraunce frayltye therfore lyghtely knowe one heretyque sayeth doth neyther worde dede thys whole realme ¶and hearynge report therin goth farther sayeth howe yt haue herde somtyme reported many heretykes yet neuer hard farre profe therin myght conscyence • uge report man man heretyque euery lyght worde man maye gyue full credēce behalfe ne reporte yt lyghtly man heretyque suche lyght tale surely thys poynte myche noted men moste spycyally dayly myny • tre sacramentes chyrche lefte happely thorough suche reportes mynystre theym somtyme dedely synne yet wolde thynke theym selfe ¶it wolde haue done well thys good man hadde geuen lyghte credence suche reportes mysse handelynge heretyques haue made hym spyrytualtye yf hym selfe therin saye trewe semeth haue geuen theym haue reported vnto hym many heretiques syth hys owne preachynge man oughte well ware howe lyghtely reporte agayne euyll lyghte reportes hathe herde slaunder one man hym selfe wold lykelyhed lyghtely haue made euyll report poynt slaunder obloquye prelate spyrytualtye therby brynge theym grudge whole temporalty vppon lyght reportes made vnto hym lyghte symple persones kynges honorable counsayle trouthe hathe ben playnely proued contrarie ¶but yet confesseth hathe herde yt sometyme reported many heretyques wolde fayne wyt hym whether suche reporte haue ben made vnto hym temporaltye saye naye tolde hym spyrytuall men may byleue hym thynke hys answere lykely wolde wene mynde betwene hym spyrytnall persones myche famylyare companye come tell hym tale semeth metely spyrytuall men mater make theyr mone vnto yf harde yt eyther temporall men besyde temporall men onely spyrytuall men dyd well wrote hys dyuysyon spyrytual men make noyse polycye yet also wolde farther wy •• whether haue herde speke heresyes place hym selfe present companye answere naye wyll preace farther vppon hym let euery man saide byleue yt thynketh yt lykely tother syde yf answere ye wolde fayne farther wyt whyther euer hym selfe wente farre wyth theym proue whether sholde hys owne rule thys chapyter haue cause shewe theyr ordynarye theym myghte sende theym ellys herynge folke speke heresyes hym toke beste alwaye owne specyall goodnesse leste myghte wyth questyonynge happe fynde yt worse folowed euer mater good counsayle saynt poule gaue nother mater nolite interrogare propter conscientiam aske questyon leste brynge scruple conscyence vsed dylygence questyonynge yt well lykely founde thys longe whyle leste wyse one ¶but yf herde speke heresye founde faute therwyth questyon asked y yt sayde lytle meruayle though neuer al england foūd one euen one thynges whyle many folke nowe fall fashyon heare heresyes talked lette talker alone whyche yet wyll yf brought court byfore iudge tell trouth wyl false forsworen thys say one special thynges whyche cryme heresye suyte ex officio whyche next chapyter folowyng laboreth • ore destroye maye euer thys man saye wyse forborne yf wolde haue • iretes swarme full heretyques lykely folowe though saye naye xl tymes haue agaynste hys boke dyuysyon well declared myne apologye hath agayn thys boke defended poynte boke dyuysyon self shal anon se god wote wyth myche worke full febly secūd part xv chapyter xv chapiter concernynge suit ex officio begynneth xlviii lefe boke holdeth ye liiii ¶and mych good christē reader may well appere poynt specyall thynge fayne wolde brynge wyt sowe opinyon mennes heddes good chaunge put awaye suit toward whiche purpose boke diuysyon bendeth laborynge fyrst many sayes brynge spyrytuall iudges suspycyon obloquy make people wene yt meruelousely dyd mych wronge cruelty mysse handle men heresye therfore shall thys poynt confute hys argumentes playne wyse lyste indyfferently rede bothe partes shall fynde cause good suffycyent vnreasonable reasōs neuer set flye ¶and fyrst bycause ye shall well se wyll wrestle darke brynge mater lyght open playne eyen wyll mater leue one word xv chapyter brynge forth wordꝭ myne thā whyle rede tone fyrste tother euyn hande shall neyther sly sleyght deceyue ¶but two thynges thys mater wyll requyre fyrste one reiecte one wyly sleyght hys goth euyn begynnynge corrupte iudgement temporall men ye redyng blynd v affecciō ¶for mater maketh two partes tone maketh spyrytualtye thys cause maketh theyrs though cōmodyte suit kepte thynge perteyned onely vnto thē tother partye maketh v temporalty wold haue put ye suit away though perleament spyrytuall men also yet al vpon one syde sure seeth wel fewe ¶but necessary consyder poynt though iudges spyrytuall yet yf suit necessary preseruacyon catholyke fayth profyte spirytuall mennes onely profyte aduauntage owne yf chaunge suit ex officio decay catholyke fayth shall folow realme losse damage vnto spyrytualtye alone harme importable vnto whole realme ¶therfore haue poynt mater euer eyen ye chaunge law yf lawe good yf chaunge better leste good comen harme whole realme harme happeneth ye gretest thyng coulde possyble take harme yf wote well euer entende faythfull trew chrysten people ¶loke therfore good reader reason myne yf fynde reasōs puttyng awaye law better kepyng catholyke fayth land ye better wyse land without minisshement fayth well cō tent ye compte thys good man bothe wyse faithfull yf fynde myne answere ye tother side yt al reasōs poynt worth one rysshe towarde profe necessary cause chaunge hys reason argumentꝭ alway therin yt eyther byelded vppon fa • se ground ellys yf make happen true yf ye fynde yet selfe reason yf men wolde vnwysely folowe myghte lawe neyther longe laste yet law made yf fynd say reason agaynst law suche ye wyll dowt thynke good reason riall reasonyng let ye law stand ¶but yf ye fynde • erther yet wote well ye shall chaūge wolde make vnder nedeles pretence preseruyng innocentes dayngeour parell proue thys hundred yere one wronged sholde cause heretykes bolde take corage encreace lacke law catholyke fayth dekaye wyll wote wel let tell thys man lacketh mater gay euer make either wyt wurse loue chrysten fayth ¶the tother thynge yt requyre shall selfe se reasonable serueth clere perceiuyng v bothe bere selfe mater shall requyre therin parcyally parte requeste indyfferent egall v bothe syth ye shall clerer therby perceyue bothe goo v bothe swarue syde fro mater hyde trouth syghte slynke lurkys lane ¶my request maye lyke take laboure payne perceyuynge trowth begynnynge peruse whole mater farre perteyneth chaunge lawe ¶reade fyrste hys owne wordes owne boke dyuysyon reade myne answere myne apologye whyche shall fynde fourtyth chapyter mater proue agaynste thys good man playne ¶in hys xv chapyter good reader wolde make men wene suffycyentely proueth thre thynges tone none hurte chaunge olde lawe secunde thynge great hurte kepe thyrde suche sample lawes thys realme resembled vnto suit ex officio resemble reason farre vnlyke ¶into thre poyntes therfore wyll deuyde thys chapyter reader may better se parte ¶i shall reherse poynt shold dyuyde • wenty partes xix partes halfe nowe clerely gone remayned y• one case wolde haue seme comen yet seuēth chapytre fyrst boke declareth hym selfe case specyall wytte witness kepte away fere elles remanaunt mannys harmes layeth agaynste law clerely gone ¶and therfore two gay case swerynge mannys deth wynnynge mānys land eschete haue place specyall point one specyall lawe yet two case suche well consydered great effect yf shold regard two case ye publyshynge wytnesses name wold seldome remedy mater yt myght well hap folke myghte hyre sholde beare suche false wytnesse thynge theym selfe lykelyhed wolde rather ¶but seynge case farre fetchynge lykelyhed seldome fortunynge lykely takē fonde yet fauour owne deuysynge lothe scrape theym excuseth dyuysynge thus yf yt sayde case fall seldome yt ought lytle pondered may sayd lyke wyse yt falleth seldome wytnesses heresye stand fere theym acc • se ¶nowe yf thys answere hys good trew yt happeth seldome wytnesses stand feare soyleth hi • owne reason hym selfe hathe cause complayne law kepe wytnesse close made serue specyal seldome case happeth feare fall ¶and therfore hys laste cause veryly shamefaste maketh though lawe made generall prohybyte men sholde haue knowledge wytnesses case ¶and poynte hys wheruppon whole mater hangeth shew sayth playn vntrew groundeth gere alwaye kepynge wytnesses close vppon playne open lye wyll thys tyme take none wytnesses agaynste hym hys owne playne open wordes seuenth chapyter hys dyuysyon lo thus good reader sayth chapyter begynneth statuta quedam decreed yf byshoppe enquerours heresye se greate daunger myghte come accusour • wytnes heresye great power theym accused maye commaunde name accusours wytnesse shall shewed bysshoppe enquerours suche lerned men called shall suffyce though shewed party indempnyte sayde accusours wytnes decreed byshoppe enquerours may enioyne haue shewed name wytnes vnto kepe close vppon payne excommunycacion dysclosynge secrete without theyr lycens surely sore law man shalbe condempned know name causers therof ¶now good chrysten reader se playnely wordes cause law specyall serueth feare wytnesses myghte stande dayngeour reason person detected man great myght power happeth seld almost neuer tyll b • well nygh paste remedy therfore se wordes hys owne wordꝭ shamfull sayth ye law generall forbedeth men sholde haue knowledge wytnesse case vpon fayth except good man se better salue sore se wolde haue wryten another poynt boke paper coste prentynge ¶but nowe saye syth se al gre • e gone saue one onely case great probable feare whyle groundeth remanaunt vppon greate open vn • rewth se well seldome gryefe lefte neuer sawe remembraunce • redde trust god neuer shall se nede euer great man •• folke neded fere condemned thys realme heresye saue onely syr hugh olde castle one tyme kyng henry v lorde cobbam yet neyther tyll thorowe heresye fell treason wolde haue ben captayne heretykes sodayne traytorouse insurreccyon ¶and therfore thys harme good man telleth v ryseth suite ex officio heresye poynte se reasonable yf happed lawe suffycyently prouyded fore yet besyde y• selde happeth realm yt foly hym speke therof yet toucheth dede suite ex officio thanne yf suit bygon pursued great man wolde fered professe hym selfe accuser thus case vtterly nothīg purpose remanaūt se also owne wordes proued grounded vpon great vntrouth therfore yt hath sayd set asyde nought let v se harme good man fyndeth ferther lo good reader therin thus sayth also syr tho denieth reason law ex de heretici • ca ad abolendam recyted vii chapyter sayde treatyse • man may dreuen • purgacyon wythout offence hym accursyd yf notably suspected yet gylty may well yet wyll condescende lawe shulde chaunged sayth fortyfyenge therof veryly thynketh whiche proued gylty heresy yet vseth maner wayes hys honest neyghbours wene one therfore theyr cōscyence dare swere well worthy penaunce truely thys merueylous persuasion mā • hulde put hys purgacyon bycause hys neyghbours dare swere heretyke ¶now good reader bycause thys good man begynneth fortifye hys worde wyth dyd sayd xl chapyter myne apologye denye man may dreuen purgacyon wythout offence hym accursed yf notably suspected yet gylty wyll fyrst brynge forth myne wordes wryten sayd chapyter afterwarde shall se whyther take suche greate holde vppon wordes wold sholde seme lo good reader wordes folio 220 may somtyme albe seld happeth heresie vpon vehement suspycyons wythout wytnesses man may put hys purgacyon penaunce also yf fayle therof whyche thynge many sholde thynke harde lawe thys pacyfyer sayth se wyse men neyther made law yet many wyse men onely wyse peraduenture many mo also nomber thys pacyfyer calleth many sayth fynde faute though alledged extra de hereticis yet law made generall counsayle veryly thynketh whyche proued gylty heresye yet vseth suche maner wayes hys honest neighbour wene one dede therfore dare swere theyr conscyence thynke hym well worthy panaūce maner byhauour wherby geueth al men occasion take hym noughty ¶now good reader thys man taketh say man may dreuen purgacyon wythout offence se well say say doth great offence well wurthy dreuē purgacyō penaūce able purge hym selfe haue vsed hym selfe lyke heretyke good folkes opiniō yt fynd good folke yt dare theyr cōsciēce swere thynke wyse saye great offence worthy dryue hym poynte good man sayth denye maye law dreuyn without offence ¶and sayth denye may dreuē therto without wytnesse wherfore praye suspycyons beyng proued wytnesses notable vehemēt wyll cause sufficyent dryue hym pourge hym selfe infamy el penaūce bryngyng hym selfe therin yf wytnessys hys expresse heretycall wordes sayth good man meruayleth yt could thynk reason shold̄ meruayle y• mater shold ashamed thinke therof telleth v good man tale onely sayth truely thys meruelous persuasion man sholde put purgacyon bycause hys neyghbours dare swere none heretyke ¶meruelouse god mannys mynde whan wrote wordes say yt shall put purgaciō bicause neighbour wyl swere nay say y• whā wytnesses sworen byfore face suspicion heresie ꝓued vpō hym thā may thordinary put hym purgacyon proue whyther wyll swere wyth hym whan wyll refuse mad man wold say shalbe put purgacyon thā whan hath fayled therof yt redy paste man speketh one perceyued pyece mater ¶for declare great offence yt vseth hym self yt none honest neighbour dare swere theyr conscyences heretyke mā taketh though sholde swere wyth hym purgacyon sholde precysely swere none heretyke theyr othe shall dede selfe thynke hys othe shall swere none heretyke byleue hath sworen trew denyeng tharticles sayd vnto hys charge lyke wageour lawe shall swere defendaunt oweth money byleue swereth treuth ¶i meruayle good fayth yt thys good man handeleth thys mater maner without tellynge meruayleth mych yt wold thynke law reasonable surely though coulde make proper reason part selfe another syde also yet wolde thynke selfe ryght vnreasonable yf shold vpō reason myn aduise counsayle realme mater concernynge conseruacyō fayth alter chaunge law made great aduyse whole generall counsayle chrystendome wherin dowte men good zele kepe innocētes trouble v twayne mych reason also haue point shewed hym apologye prouisyon made ye saw ad abolendā also made generall counsayle ye tale letteth go though herde ¶but cometh forth wyth worde two ferther fawte law eyther man vnderstandeth meneth ellys herd man thynke yt meneth wel wordꝭ veryly law theyr othe case shulde accepted sayde chapyter ad abolendam yf man notably suspected heresye shall purge hym selfe wyl thordynarye accursed purgacyon hy • neyghbour wyll serue lette euery man therfore consyder whether sayd law indysferent yf lette put theyr hande haue broken thynke veryly shall deserue great thanke god yf tourne indyfferent waye nowe vnder thys maner moost innocent man may malyce reported suspected heresye dede dreuen hys purgacyon accursed another law yf case indurate mynde stande accursed yere shalbe punished heretike law extra de hereticis ca exc • municamu • ¶this prouysyon good reader yt speketh whyche lawe ad abolendam recited v boke decretalis tytle de hereticis yt suspecte shold purge selfe arbitrement discrecion thordynary haue sayed afterward loked vppon alowed generall counsayle called consiliū latranense euery man may soone perceyue wyll well consyder paragraffe excō municamꝰ afterward tytle ye law saith qui inuēti fuerit sola suspitione notabiles nisi statim innocētiā suā congrua purgatione mōstrauerint wordꝭ congrua purgatione referred vnto tother law ad abolendā therof made byfore bothe appereth doctours wryte vpō ye lawes also hym yt wyl cōsider wel wel appereth y• self text ye paragraf excō rehersed part wordes law • ad abolendam wherby may se yt counsayle loked vpon lawe saye prouisyon man calleth vnreasonable onely made pope lucius iii also made agayne ratificacyō pope innocent ye iii hose generall coūsaile rede story wyll shall fynde bothe platiua cronica cronicarū pope lucius thys pope innocēt vertuouse men ben reasō therfore yt good man sith fyndeth point gret fawt ye wittꝭ good pope al thē y• membres generall counsayle wyttꝭ al chrysten regyons haue vsed allowed yt lawe good euer synnys reason wolde say sholde leste haue layed reason wherfore ye lawe please hym whiche though proued gysty dede yet proued suspecte shold purge hym selfe tharbitrement thordynarye wytte suche maner wyse thordynary sholde thynke conuenyent vpō qualytees yt person cyrcūstaūces ye cause cōsydered ¶suppose yt none maner purgacion neyghbours swerynge wyth hym wordꝭ ad arbitriū epi writen law yet reason accepte oth euer maner man wolde hym selfe deuyse handes hym selfe lyste appoynt maner folke euer hym selfe wolde brynge ¶nay syr may yt shalbe good cause somtyme place thordynary sholde putte man kynde purgacion yf dyd neuer noughty shold sure compurgatours peraduenture mo inough ¶for hath ben sene many cūtreys ere somtyme england euyll precher prechyng playne opē heresyes shold yet myght haue ben put purgacyō haue lacked none handes lay boke hym neuer spake suche wordes ye wordꝭ opē playn heresye ye law hath ꝓuided way ye remedy good inough ¶but thā haue ben prechers ere ye techyng playne heresy theyr familiar secretely wold prech wyse abrode theyr wordꝭ shold haue two sens one bote serue eyther legge like shypmans hose shold tempered peple shold haue occasyon alway take wurst hym selfe yf examined wold say thordinary swere neuer ment beste ¶now whan shold good wytnesses appere yt maner peple toke mych harme therby alwaye toke wordꝭ thought mēt thē y• purposed set forth aduaūce thyngꝭ yt stark heresy dede yf thordinary shold thā appoint cōpurgatours purge suspiciō suspiciōs neuer vehemēt shold lacke cō purgatours purge hym self euery weke thā dyd many good symple folke takyng euē ment shold fall heresyes y• whyle wene preched styll yt byleue ye way perell ¶and therfore wise men made ye law left ye thyng thordinarys discreciō assigne hym proued suspect heresy kynde purgacyon cyrcumstaunces person peple tyme shall requyre ¶and therfore wyll thordynary man suspecte somtyme assygne hym purge suspycyon yt lewd maner prechynge fallen greate hurte herers shall openly confesse yt heresyes people toke hym mene salse syes dede openly shall deteste swere byleueth swere neither ment teche theym neuer mynded yt mā shold take hym neuer wold afterward teche hold heresy abiure thē euer ¶and yet ferther purgacyō suspiciō ordynary myght also enioyne hym certayn thynges suche maye declare clereli yt mind open prechyng agaynste selfe heresyes doynge suche thynges heresyes dyd stande agaynste ¶and purgacyon thys good shall yf wolde preache thynges agayne though vsed agayne nother wyly fashyon yet wolde audyence thynke thus many hadde mynde good eyther man meaneth nowe wordes teache v poynt hym selfe hath abiured lette v lerne thynge hym wolde wyse shold elles meaneth • ache yt v styll al abiuracion wherfore sholde madde byleue false wreche yt wold make v byleue thynge trewe whyche hym selfe hath openly cōfessed sworen false ¶but wyll happely good man say abiuracyon perylouse iubardye relapse parell deth relapse vppon euery abiuracyon trouth abiured vppon thynges proued maketh hym sleyghtly vehemently suspected yf fall heresye putteth hym selfe parell fall fyre good reason yt yt man may tyme suspecte felony reason sore presumpcyons yt though man saw hym yt hym selfe neuer confesse yt saye swere neuer hadde yt yet may founden gyltye yt theruppon hāged yt haue wrōge ¶and thus prouysyon purgacyon dyscrecyon ordynarye truste vnreasonable vnreasonable made yt vnreasonable yt ratified al vnresonable yt thys two thre hūdred yere haue accepted allowed yt yt maye nowe stande thys good mā ny leue daye well yt hath standen whyle yet one thīg yt taketh thing sore thā sayth nother law proued suspect refuse pourge hym self discrecyon thordynary hys con • umacy excommunycate case yf obdurate harte stande accursed whole yere shalbe punyshed heretyke y sayth law extra de hereticis capitulo excommunicamus ¶this prouisyon made tolde sayde generall counsayle bringeth forth though yt sore thyng cruell yt dede fauorable sauynge wyll doth go fynd fautes doynges many mych better myche wytte elles could lay lytle better cause proue prouysyon ouer fauorable euer good man shall fynde whyle lyueth proue prouysyon sore surely beynge proued suspect refuseth reasonable maner purge hym self therof ordynarye shall dyscrecyon assygne hym whych must lawe reason iudge hym self sheweth hym self lytle force care though folke wene heretyque whych thyng sore aggreueth suspycyon veryly one dede whē wyll rather one accursed suche suspycyon yet purge clere hym selfe yet encreaseth ye suspycyon twyse sore fynally rather purge suspycyon contynueth excommunycated whole yere neuer wyll purged whyle yf maye haue yt accepted suche faynte fashyon hym selfe lyste offre suspycyon heresyes sore vehement tourne suche dealynge pleyne open vyolent reason none rekened playne heretyque dede whome tolerate longe doth somtyme lytle good syth law fauour chyrche shall preserue temporall handes shold lawe onely vpon theyr deteccyon tourne theyr offre mekely shewe good token ryghte harty repentaunce wyll let man thinclinacyon towarde pytye preseruynge lyfe man euer seme penytent yet surely chyrch receyueth agayne man obstynate dealynge wyth abydynge excomunicate contempnyng great curse whole yere rather wolde purge suspycyon heresye yf may purge swete wyll proueth hym self last haue ben heretyque longe whyle wold retourne euer drawe bakke yf thordynary receyue hym grace agayne kepe hym styll preserue seculare handes wyll saye doth wrong fyndynge hym yet repentaunte fayne wolde se hym saued ¶but yet wythout doute farre se thordynarye saue mannys lyfe pytye strecheth wyth teth lawe reason farre euyn scantely holde ¶and therfore lawes beynge suche made ratyfyed whole generall counsayle accepted vsed longe thorow al chrystendome thys good man cometh forth vppon bare reason bare euer herd yet lyfe bycause onely innocente may somtyme take harme whyche may happen vppon lawe euer world make wherby shalbe deuysed punyshment euyl folke byddeth euery man cōsyder nowe whyther law iuste byddeth euery mā put theyr handes haue yt broken make better sayeth thynketh shall haue great thanke god therfore request better effecte euyn agaynste euery wyse mannes reason well approued hytherto euery man shold mater eyther trust vnto el lest wise euery man owne stede better old law make new mych worse deuise folowed appereth playnely sholde heresyes sholde grow vp heyght catholyque fayth decaye god saue v frome thanke god shortely shold wyth dealynge deserue ¶thus haue good reader se clerely confuted good mā ny answere bothe pryncypa •• poyntes whyche tone wherin mynded shewe heresye suyte offyce myghte lefte leuyng shold none harme folow catholyque faythe bycause heretyques myght well come correccyon waye open accuser maner suyte ¶but poynte haue sene clerely deuyse wolde neuer serue mater yt lykely mynyshe thys realme catholyque fayth encrease heresyes thindygnacyon god sore fered therby folowe theron realme fall trouble besynesse insurreccion rebellyous • heretyques chaunge law bene suffred grow countreys haue ben late realme ere nere lyke haue ben thauoyding lyke parell fall afterwarde yt prouyded parlyament great polycye better repressyng heresyes fortyfye lawe gyue thordynaryes yet greater power maynteyne yt wyth temporall assystēce make yt strong ¶his secunde poynte shew kepynge law sholde growe great harme bycause law vnreasonable sayth innocentes may come trouble therby wythout offence ¶this parte howe properly thys good man hath proued haue sene also therin full whole confuted readeth yt agayne suppose greatly lyke ¶now two thus handeled cometh thyrde poynte whyche though graunted hym gether yet neuer nere yt poynt suche yf wynne thanne maketh parte playne tother syde yf loste wanne yet myne playne inough stronge inough part wyth fyrste poynt alone yf leuynge suit office shold folow thencreace heretikes euery man thynke wyt hath may well se wolde though wold harme happē somtyme therof yet must harme reason rather borne ¶but come good reader vnto thyrde poynt whyche yf wan together coulde lytell serue hym ye shall se hym yet goddes grace wynne hym neuer pyece ¶the thyrde poynt good reader myn apology se well self entendeth nothynge ellys en • emple comen lawes thys realme shew spyrytuall law whyche man wolde proue vnreasonable • de proued man y countrey hym self lyeth somtyme styll pryson tyll retourne yf returned good wyt yf maner purged delyuered yet payeth fee ere go yf retourned noughte vse iuges bynde hym hys good aberynge som tyme suertyes wyth hym suche theyr dyscrecyon allowe lye styll tyll fynde theym somtyme myche penaunce tone spyrytuall iudge • oyneth tother tone cometh barre openly tother consystorye somtyme hys feters waye good pyece fagotte bysydes lye lenger tone mannys legges fagotte tothers sholdre yet y remedye bothe must done tone court tother ellys stede one harme whych hym deserueth yt happeth seldome seldome sure heresye thefte myche seldome ye shall haue tenne tymes harme happen dayly folke innocēt innocentes many made nocentes destruccyon theym selfe bothe goodes bodye soule ¶ thys pyece lo good reader thys good mannys answere goeth mayntenaunce sayde suyte ex officio resembleth arestyng suspecyon felonye suertye good aberynge indytementes wheruppon men put answere commen lawe farre resemblance varye suyte ex officio place openeth yt hym selfe yet playne declaracyon therin shall saye lytle farther mater fyrst arres • ynge suspycyon felonye yt dede olde lawe thys realme suspycyon felonye man may arrested doth arres • e hym vppon reasonable cause doth suspecte hym yt generall rule shall neuer put answere vpon arreste proclamacyon shalbe made yf man wyll lay thynge agaynst hym suspected shal herde yf none cōe shalbe delyuered without fine • punyshmēt good exhortaciō iudges shall take good hede howe ordereth hym selfe tyme come mayster lykeneth penaunce suche man hath ben pryson vppon suspycyon felonye delyuered proclamacyon bearynge fagotte heresye sayth one shal come openly barre consystory sometyme fetter shall • ey good pece fagot besydes lye lenger one mannys legges fagotte mannys shulder reherseth howe lye many tymes lenger pryson heresye eyther suspycyon felonye good aberynge ouer dare say hadde wel leuer abyde payne thryse acquyted proclamacyon peraduēture ofter thē one beare fagot heresy ¶howe goeth nowe good reader thys answere thys good man vnto purpose proue trouble hym y arrested vppon suspycyon felonye vnlyke trouble hym y sued ex officio heresye touchynge poynte resemble theym ¶the point ye wote wel sor whyche speke tharrestyng suspycyon felonye shew lyke wyse yt may happen man heresye fall trouble sometyme though none heretike ī dede • may yt happen man somtyme troubled vppon suspycyon fel • nye though felon dede yet bothe tone lawe necessarye tother neyther bothe maye forborne hathe good man proued v contrarye se well hath hathe perdye proued vnlyke ¶he weneth sayth somewhat whan telleth v vpon tharrestynge vppon suspycyon felonye shall put answere tyll indighted hys trouble lesse lye pryson tyll borne vppe wyth rope ¶and therfore dyd place onely shew • innocent maye arrestynge felonye happe haue myche harme yt innocent arrested heresye maye happen haue sometyme also mych harme fyrst tyme answere ¶after haue weth ye iudges spyrytuall court folysshe leuer medle man saue onely vppon suche open inquisycyon indyghtementes felonye auoydynge obloquy sauyng necessyte compelleth take thys way suspected beginnyng whan toke hym yet yf fynde xamynacyon suspicyons clered putteth hym ferther busynesse also yf fully clered remayne token suspycyon whych thynke good pourge hym ye othe hym self cōpour gatours hym putteth hym yt purgacion vnto penaunce neyther yf yt wel ꝓued suspiciōs vehement though proue precysely ye dede yet make euery man hereth thē none wyse thynke wyll ordynary cause hym abiure yt rather purge hym suspycyō styll nought afterwarde styll wolde nought yt vsyng hym self wyse though penaunce hath right ¶but case suspiciō purged saith vntrew penaunce ¶now concernynge good aberynge awarded iustyces answereth yt trew sayth vnlyke vnto mater bycause iustyces sayth whā hath long lyen pryson maye theyr dyscrecyon yf fynd suertyes ward wrytte de gestu et fama ¶this half answere scant mych neyther fyrst hym selfe sayth wryt maye sende ye man hath long lyen pryson man yet wythout presentement open accusour hath longe lyenge pryson meane whyle hys • uyl demenure home among hys neyghbours wherof durste openly make complaynt thys doth se thys good man deny whych purpose inough ¶but saith ferther sayth may award wrytte yf wyll wherin implyeth yf wyl may vpon good dyscrecyon lette hym yet lye styll let wrytte alone hath therfore putte one poynt ferther ¶but yet hath good man one stoppe gappe styll proue alwaye sample lyke suyte ex officio men put answere vpō arreste imprysoment vppon̄ good aberynge man shall neuer putte answere ¶for answere euasyon wyll aske good man pryson vpō good aberyng shall neuer put answere whyther profyte losse losse puttyng answere maketh ye mater resemblyng mych strong yf good man dare answere yt profite wyll praye hym put felow choyse yf hym selfe chose better let hym lye styl ¶this se good reader man sayth nay vpō good aberynge dyscressyon iustyces wrytte de gestu fama man maye lye longe pryson peraduēture euer trouth trow happeth ¶and yet neither good man say suppose man ellys maye somtyme happe possybylyte informacyon wronge thynge lykely happe often yf sholde suche may happys put away yt ordre whiche order necessyte brought vp wolde mych myschyefe grow many great harmes wold thā happe ī dede ¶now towchyng sayde kynges counsayle vsed also somtyme vppon great secrete informacion put folke busynes dishonesty letted laye sample myne owne dede whyle chauncellour self puttyng cōmyssyō theyr vntrouth part answereth greate deale lesse thā halfe parte neuer deale men content take fashyō answerynge let man make agaynste many bokes wyll putte mater lyst shall neuer nede study mych answere day man getteth hym fyre shaketh hatte shoure rayne nowe yt often happeth man cometh shoure ouersyght though somtyme chaūs aduenture surely though somtyme yt happe man accused endyghted malyce • lykelyhed whyche happed hym chaunce faute therin yet happeth yt comparyson selde partye demeanure hym selfe gyueth occasyō folke haue hym suspected ¶in pyece purpose good reders se shewe lyke wise seldome happeth partye falleth trouble without defaute hym selfe commen generall lawe maye seldome specyall happes forborne pyece lo good man answereth thus mayster sayth yet farther vppon better broughte lyghte lacke thys good man hath suffycyent answere lo good reader therin farther wordes nowe yf thys pacyfyer saye yet y leste wyse temporall inge open cause apperyng whereuppon men endyghtement leste wyse open cause apperynge wheruppon man maye se iudge calleth hym hys owne mynde vppon mater broughte vnto hym wolde graunte hym thys dede good ease temporall iudge kepe hym oute thynge proue well shall se saye wolde haue graunted allway thys good man wold allwaye therwythall haue tolde hym yet tale hys hadde nothyge touched poynte alwaye tale man indyghted yf mater dede vntrew neuer nerer knowledge accuser gete amendes therby called offyce heresye byfore spyrytuall iudge nowe sayth whyther answere poynt yt mēt one ynch yet nerer lo good reader hys proper answere thē bycause cā none otherwise cōfesse great dynersyte betwyxte put answere ex officio putte answere kynges iustyces vppon indytementes common lawe iudges haue suffycyent apparant mater put theym answere vppon none spyrytuall iudge vppon dyspleasure may yt ex officio yf wyll therfore goeth yet farther sayeth xii men maye yet make man called gyltye yf dysposed trouth yt may indyte man absent also gyltye vntrewe yf wyll yet suche case xii men knowen yt also compelled vppon inquyrye maye vppon therto assygned also partye vppon theyre verdyte shall put answere theym yt vpon suyte ex officio dyfference bycause yt lyke indyghtementes poynte therfore heresye eyther clerely nought ellys lest wyse yt somwhat better sholde neuer put man answere heresye eyther vppon open accusacyon psentement ex officio wolde haue men comenly called eyther accusacyō presentemēt theyr senys endyghtemētes comō lawe lyefe thynge se thys pacyfyer sholde say thus thys way called wolde haue called wolde haue called suche order myght sure sholde neuer called accuse folke openly heresye euery man hath experyence inough ye shall seldome fynde man wyll yf iudge shold set officer court therto wythout perell expensys thys way way one effecte presentemē te endyghtemētes effecte wolde come concernynge heresye ye se profe trowe metely well redy thys thyng well knowen vnto euery man euery sene euery sessyon peace euery sessyon gaole delyuery euery lete thorough realme fyrste thynge iury haue gyuen charge heresye thys thorow whole realme many presentemē te made whole yere wene seuen yere one suppose man yf spyrytuall ruler wolde preche heresye yf ment spyrituall ruler chrystendome wolde haue admitted case none wyse men put admitte case impossyble se myghte ensew theron yf possyble saynt poule putteth apperynge wherfore saue onely cause euery man may spye wold haue sene place lefte vntowched maner moste parte togyther boke towched thre chapyters haue tother syde lefte one pyece vnproued selfe spake thynge perteyned vnto ¶and therfore begynnyng xxii chapyter symkyn salem geueth hys sentence vppon sayde answere sayde apologye alloweth sayd answere well thynketh yf consydered onely myche hath lefte vnanswered mych owne wordes vndefended whyche nothynge hath towched ouer febly hath defended thynges hath towched salem beynge indyfferent ben like haue allowed lytell ¶for settynge asyde whyle remanaunt yf go pryncypal poynt alone wherin laboreth chaūge put awaye good lawes ye chaūge wherof suche deuyseth decaye catholyke fayth encreace heresyes wolde folowe poynt alone say laye agaynst hym comen cōsent realm layeth reasō agaynst laye agaynste hym consent ye generall coūsayle agaynst layeth owne reason lay agaynst hym generall approbaciō chrystē realmes agaynst layeth reason hys owne irrefragable reason layth agaynst surely se lawes innocēt may sometyme take wrong agaynste reason lay hym yf reason sholde stande agaynst malefactours could law stande laye agaynst also deuyces yf folowed encreace heresyes many innocentes must nedes take mych wronge ¶to thys answereth wyll answere nowe salem seeth answere seeth al weigth mater hangeth vpon sym salem geueth sentence hath answered well surely yf suche answeryng well wote whyche way man myght answere yll ¶and therfore symkyn salem sayth yf good man wyll wyll cause frende hys answere remanaunt may good man myche frēdly tourne yf make hys frende answere better fyrst good man hath answered allredy yt yf lyste thus geue ouer thys assaye saye better pyece let theym goddes name hardely go yf saye thynge metely mater wyll put frende payne make answere leasure cōuenient shal answere selfe say well wyll let saye say wronge wyll lette tell theym tother syde yf go better worke nerer mater thys man hath done shall hym poynt beleue hym yf sayde therin trew fautes onely hys owne whyche haue often sayde myche rather thynke sotle shrewes haue deceyued hym ¶and besyde sondry thynges lede thynke one stronge thynge y thys euery man maye well se hys boke suche haue resorted hym tell hym suche thynges vnder sayes put oute agayne haue alwaye tolde hym euyll neuer told good misse handlynge heresyes haue euer tolde hym wyll serue hym ¶for fyrste haue sayed ofter one redy thynges comen lawe chaunged yf shall come therof harme thanne good yf yt happen one innocent take harme lawe shall fyue one take harme chaunge ¶more ouer yf sholde cause chaunge tēporall lawes y wytte bycause innocent maye somtyme take harme must chaunge reason olde vsed lawe man maye arrested remayne pryson tyll fynde suertyes peace vppon bare othe hys enmye sayth ferde hym law may tyme innocent take harme yet muste lawe stande yf well ellys shall chaūge mo innocentes take harme ¶what trouble haue many men walys compelled bounden peace bothe selfe theyr seruauntes frendes yet order necessary many lordshyppes yt maye forborne ¶and surely yf fall chaungynge lawes vpon ye symple groūd muste chaunge many wolde well ¶bysydes thys yf men sholde reforme chaunge lawe bycause innocent maye somtyme take harme therby must haue chaunged chaunge yt yet agayne chaunge yet chaunge yt agayne forth chaūge chaunge neuer cease chaungynge tyll worlde chaunged daye dome neuer wyttes yt make one penall lawe suche none innocent may take harme therby ¶how yt yf newe lawe drawen putte forthe made agaynst myschiefe wold el mych harme good reason yt take excepcyon byl shewe innocent • myghte myche harmed thys poynt therwyth prouyde remedye putte lawe stoppe many gappes coulde spyed ye yf law made men foud notable harme good folke myche wronged lawe suche eyther myghte forborne el meanes founde chaunged better good reason wold make prouysyon ¶but surely come forth thys man cometh agaynste good lawes well made great authoryte longe approued thorow whole corp chrystendome thys realme ratyfyed specyally parlyament vppon profe wythout great grounde cause euer synnys founden profytable preseruacyon fayth proued se necessary vpon thys mannes deuyces without great encreace heresyes forborne neuer chaunged eyther strayghter ellys wurse come forth appeasynge dyuysyon fyrste slaunder maye make dyuysyon labour chaunge lawes vpon
